It goes without saying that the literature on the various aspects of the UN is vast and the suggestions provided here necessarily 
limited. Some of the best general accounts covering most aspects of the world organization include: Frederick H. Gareau, [3mThe 
United Nations and Other International Institutions: A Critical Analysis [0m(Chicago: Burnham, 2002); Thomas G. Weiss, David P. 
Forsythe, and Roger A. Coate, [3mThe United Nations and Changing World Politics [0m(Boulder, CO: Westview, 2004). One can also benefit 
from reviewing the UNโs own [3mBasic Facts about the United Nations [0m(New York: United Nations, 2004, or later edition) and Thomas G. 
Weiss and Sam Daws, [3mThe Oxford Handbook on the United Nations [0m(New York: Oxford University Press, 2007). For a readable general 
history and evaluations of the UN readers can turn to Paul Kennedy, [3mThe Parliament of Man: The Past, Present and Future of the 
United Nations [0m(New York: Random House, 2007).
